###xml 154 160 154 160 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">deltaC</italic>
###xml 228 233 228 233 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">ta52b</sup>
###xml 225 233 225 233 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">mib<sup>ta52b</sup></italic>
###xml 235 244 235 244 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pone-0000302-g005">Figure 5C</xref>
###xml 246 253 246 253 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="table" rid="pone-0000302-t001">Table 1</xref>
###xml 281 287 281 287 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">tit446</sup>
###xml 278 287 278 287 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">des<sup>tit446</sup></italic>
###xml 289 298 289 298 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pone-0000302-g005">Figure 5D</xref>
###xml 300 307 300 307 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="table" rid="pone-0000302-t001">Table 1</xref>
###xml 342 345 342 345 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">DBM</sup>
###xml 335 345 335 345 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">X-Su(H)<sup>DBM</sup></italic>
###xml 369 378 369 378 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pone-0000302-g005">Figure 5E</xref>
###xml 380 387 380 387 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="table" rid="pone-0000302-t001">Table 1</xref>
###xml 447 453 447 453 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">deltaC</italic>
###xml 470 476 470 476 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">deltaC</italic>
###xml 582 593 582 593 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">X-Su(H)/Ank</italic>
###xml 649 655 649 655 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">deltaC</italic>
###xml 717 726 717 726 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pone-0000302-g005">Figure 5F</xref>
###xml 728 735 728 735 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="table" rid="pone-0000302-t001">Table 1</xref>
###xml 767 773 767 773 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">deltaC</italic>
###xml 855 861 855 861 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">ascl1a</italic>
###xml 866 871 866 871 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">notch</italic>
We also manipulated Notch activity to see whether deltaC expression is negatively regulated. Compared to wild-type embryos (Figure 5B), we found that the deltaC-positive area in the ventral ectoderm was 5.7-fold increased in mibta52b (Figure 5C; Table 1), 5.5-fold increased in destit446 (Figure 5D; Table 1) and 3.9-fold increased in X-Su(H)DBM mRNA-injected embryos (Figure 5E; Table 1), whose Notch activity was compromised due to a failure of deltaC ubiquitination, deltaC ligand expression, and transmission of the Notch signal through Su(H), respectively. On the contrary, in X-Su(H)/Ank mRNA-injected embryos whose Notch signal was enhanced, deltaC expression in the ventral ectoderm was completely abolished (Figure 5F; Table 1). Therefore, we confirmed that deltaC expression by epidermal IC progenitors is positively and negatively regulated by ascl1a and notch, respectively.
###end p 27
###begin title 28
###xml 25 31 25 31 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">foxi3a</italic>
###xml 36 42 36 42 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">foxi3b</italic>
Reciprocal Regulation of foxi3a and foxi3b Expressions by a Positive Regulatory Loop
###end title 28
###begin p 29
###xml 0 6 0 6 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">foxi3a</italic>
###xml 33 39 33 39 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">foxi3b</italic>
###xml 69 78 69 78 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pone-0000302-g001">Figure 1N</xref>
###xml 129 135 129 135 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">foxi3a</italic>
###xml 140 146 140 146 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">foxi3b</italic>
###xml 233 240 233 240 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">foxi3a,</italic>
###xml 240 249 240 249 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pone-0000302-g006">Figure 6A</xref>
###xml 251 257 251 257 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">foxi3b</italic>
###xml 259 268 259 268 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pone-0000302-g006">Figure 6D</xref>
###xml 285 291 285 291 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">foxi3a</italic>
###xml 328 334 328 334 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">foxi3b</italic>
###xml 346 355 346 355 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pone-0000302-g006">Figure 6C</xref>
###xml 364 370 364 370 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">foxi3b</italic>
###xml 410 416 410 416 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">foxi3a</italic>
###xml 445 454 445 454 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pone-0000302-g006">Figure 6F</xref>
###xml 529 535 529 535 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">foxi3a</italic>
###xml 540 546 540 546 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">foxi3b</italic>
###xml 584 590 584 590 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">foxi3a</italic>
###xml 654 663 654 663 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pone-0000302-g006">Figure 6H</xref>
###xml 697 706 697 706 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pone-0000302-g006">Figure 6G</xref>
###xml 741 747 741 747 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">foxi3b</italic>
###xml 787 793 787 793 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">foxi3a</italic>
###xml 817 826 817 826 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pone-0000302-g006">Figure 6E</xref>
###xml 843 849 843 849 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">foxi3a</italic>
###xml 889 895 889 895 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">foxi3b</italic>
###xml 925 934 925 934 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pone-0000302-g006">Figure 6B</xref>
###xml 971 977 971 977 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">foxi3a</italic>
###xml 1005 1011 1005 1011 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">foxi3b</italic>
###xml 1025 1031 1025 1031 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">foxi3a</italic>
###xml 1036 1042 1036 1042 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">foxi3b</italic>
foxi3a is activated earlier than foxi3b in epidermal IC progenitors (Figure 1N). We tested the hierarchical relationship between foxi3a and foxi3b by both loss- and gain-of-function approaches in 5-s embryos. Compared to wild types (foxi3a,Figure 6A; foxi3b, Figure 6D), we found that foxi3a expression was almost unaffected in foxi3b morphants (Figure 6C), while foxi3b expression was completely abolished in foxi3a morphants at the 5-s stage (Figure 6F). However, as development proceeded, it was still possible to detect some foxi3a- or foxi3b-positive epidermal IC progenitors in foxi3a morphants, although their relative number was greatly reduced (Figure 6H) when compared to the wild type (Figure 6G). For the gain-of-function assay, foxi3b expression was 6.1-fold upregulated in foxi3a mRNA-injected embryos (Figure 6E). Surprisingly, foxi3a expression was 2-fold upregulated when foxi3b mRNA was forcedly expressed (Figure 6B). This result suggests that, first, foxi3a is genetically upstream of foxi3b and, second, foxi3a and foxi3b can be reciprocally regulated by a positive feedback loop.
###end p 29
###begin p 30
###xml 146 151 146 151 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">gata2</italic>
###xml 156 161 156 161 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">gata3</italic>
###xml 161 165 161 165 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0000302-Read1">[44]</xref>
###xml 384 390 384 390 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">foxi3a</italic>
###xml 392 401 392 401 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pone-0000302-g006">Figure 6A</xref>
###xml 407 413 407 413 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">foxi3b</italic>
###xml 415 424 415 424 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pone-0000302-g006">Figure 6D</xref>
###xml 529 535 529 535 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">foxi3a</italic>
###xml 542 543 542 543 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">n</italic>
###xml 551 560 551 560 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pone-0000302-g006">Figure 6E</xref>
###xml 565 571 565 571 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">foxi3b</italic>
###xml 578 579 578 579 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">n</italic>
###xml 587 596 587 596 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pone-0000302-g006">Figure 6B</xref>
###xml 859 865 859 865 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">foxi3a</italic>
###xml 870 876 870 876 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">foxi3b</italic>
###xml 26 35 <span type="species:ncbi:7955">zebrafish</span>
The epidermal ectoderm of zebrafish gastrula can be divided into three subdomains along the A/P axis according to the differential expressions of gata2 and gata3[44]. After completion of convergent extension, these three subdomains give rise to the epidermis covering the cephalic (zone I), trunk (zone II), and tail (zone III), respectively. For wild-type 5-s embryos, we found that foxi3a (Figure 6A) and foxi3b (Figure 6D) were restrictedly expressed within the epidermal IC domain (corresponding to zone II). However, either foxi3a (50%, n = 255, Figure 6E) or foxi3b (35%, n = 223, Figure 6B) misexpression was sufficient to generate extra epidermal IC progenitors at ectopic sites of zones I and III at the 5-s stage. Moreover, the generating potential of ectopic epidermal ICs gradually declined from zones I to III. This result demonstrated that both foxi3a and foxi3b are sufficient to specify the IC identity and that the entire epidermal ectoderm is permissive for epidermal IC formation.
###end p 30
###begin p 31
###xml 119 125 119 125 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">foxi3a</italic>
###xml 129 135 129 135 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">foxi3b</italic>
###xml 278 285 278 285 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">in situ</italic>
###xml 305 312 305 312 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">atp1b1b</italic>
###xml 317 321 317 321 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">ca2a</italic>
###xml 339 345 339 345 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">foxi3a</italic>
###xml 355 361 355 361 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">foxi3b</italic>
###xml 533 539 533 539 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">foxi3a</italic>
###xml 610 616 610 616 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">foxi3a</italic>
###xml 690 691 690 691 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">n</italic>
###xml 713 714 713 714 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">n</italic>
###xml 836 845 836 845 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pone-0000302-g007">Figure 7B</xref>
###xml 890 896 890 896 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">foxi3b</italic>
###xml 946 947 946 947 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">n</italic>
###xml 955 964 955 964 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pone-0000302-g007">Figure 7C</xref>
###xml 1039 1045 1039 1045 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">foxi3b</italic>
###xml 1079 1080 1079 1080 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">n</italic>
###xml 1087 1096 1087 1096 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pone-0000302-g007">Figure 7F</xref>
###xml 1302 1309 1302 1309 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">atp1b1b</italic>
###xml 1314 1318 1314 1318 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">ca2a</italic>
###xml 1335 1351 1335 1351 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pone-0000302-g007">Figure 7E and 7F</xref>
###xml 1411 1417 1411 1417 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">foxi3a</italic>
###xml 1438 1444 1438 1444 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">foxi3b</italic>
###xml 1607 1613 1607 1613 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">foxi3a</italic>
###xml 1618 1624 1618 1624 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">foxi3b</italic>
In addition to functioning as epidermal IC determinants, it is not clear whether the unusually high level of exogenous foxi3a or foxi3b is related to the precocious differentiation of epidermal IC progenitors. Therefore, we addressed this event by performing fluorescent double in situ hybridization with atp1b1b and ca2a probes in either foxi3a mRNA- or foxi3b mRNA-injected embryos at the 5-s and 24-hpf stages. In a normal condition, NaRCs and HRCs did not differentiate until the 14- and 18-s stages, respectively. However, when foxi3a mRNA was misexpressed, we found that the elevated expression level of foxi3a was sufficient to promote precocious differentiation of both NaRCs (73%, n = 171) and HRCs (4%, n = 171) not only within the epidermal IC domain but also in the ectopic sites of the cephalic epidermis at the 5-s stage (Figure 7B). Only NaRCs differentiated precociously in foxi3b mRNA-misexpressed embryos at the 5-s stage (16%, n = 190, Figure 7C). But at 24 hpf, ectopic HRCs could be found in the cephalic epidermis in foxi3b mRNA-misexpressing embryos (52%, n = 60, Figure 7F). In addition, we also noted that ectopic epidermal ICs occurred at the expense of the epidermal SC fate, since the epidermal SC marker of P63 was completely abolished in some regions where high levels of atp1b1b and ca2a were expressed (Figure 7E and 7F, highlighted by arrows). Taken together, we concluded that foxi3a is more potent than foxi3b in promoting IC differentiation in wild-type embryos, and that the timing of NaRC and HRC differentiation is strongly dependent on the relative concentrations of foxi3a and foxi3b accumulated in epidermal IC progenitors.
###end p 31

###xml 26 32 26 32 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">foxi3a</italic>

###xml 662 668 662 668 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">foxi3b</italic>

###xml 887 893 887 893 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">foxi3a</italic>
###xml 897 903 897 903 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">foxi3b</italic>
###xml 969 975 969 975 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">foxi3a</italic>
###xml 980 986 980 986 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">foxi3b</italic>
###xml 1045 1051 1045 1051 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">foxi3a</italic>
###xml 1056 1062 1056 1062 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">foxi3b</italic>
###xml 1149 1155 1149 1155 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">foxi3a</italic>

###xml 1194 1205 1194 1205 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">X-Su(H)/Ank</italic>
###xml 1214 1218 1214 1218 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">bmp7</italic>
###xml 1244 1255 1244 1255 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">X-Su(H)/Ank</italic>
###xml 1310 1311 1310 1311 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">n</italic>
###xml 1567 1574 1567 1574 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">atp1b1b</italic>
###xml 1579 1591 1579 1591 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">ca2a in situ</italic>
###xml 1647 1648 1647 1648 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">n</italic>
###xml 1656 1665 1656 1665 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pone-0000302-g008">Figure 8C</xref>
###xml 1707 1713 1707 1713 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">foxi3a</italic>
###xml 1792 1793 1792 1793 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">n</italic>
###xml 1815 1816 1815 1816 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">n</italic>
###xml 1861 1870 1861 1870 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pone-0000302-g008">Figure 8D</xref>
###xml 1873 1879 1873 1879 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">foxi3b</italic>
###xml 1941 1942 1941 1942 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">n</italic>
###xml 1971 1972 1971 1972 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">n</italic>
###xml 2016 2025 2016 2025 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pone-0000302-g008">Figure 8E</xref>
Based on the differential expressions of foxi3a and foxi3b in differentiating NaRC (foxi3bhigh) and HRC (foxi3ahigh/foxi3blow) lineages, we speculated that they might have distinct functions in promoting the differentiation of NaRCs and HRCs. However, according to the misexpression data performed in wild-type embryos, it was difficult to distinguish the distinct functions between foxi3a and foxi3b in promoting NaRC and HRC differentiation. Actually, the misexpression results obtained in the wild-type background should be carefully interpreted when both Foxi3a and Foxi3b activities are present, because the positive regulatory loop will amplify downstream foxi3b when only foxi3a is misexpressed. In the same manner, the positive regulatory loop can also amplify upstream foxi3a when only foxi3b is misexpressed. Therefore, in the wild-type background, regardless of misexpression foxi3a or foxi3b, it will turn out to be a combinatorial effect derived from both foxi3a and foxi3b misexpression. In order to differentiate the functions of foxi3a and foxi3b more precisely, we sought to create a genetic background which contains no endogenous foxi3a or foxi3b expression by misexpressing X-Su(H)/Ank mRNA or bmp7 MO. When a high level of X-Su(H)/Ank mRNA (500 pg per embryo) was misexpressed, about 45% (n = 210) of the injected embryos showed a reduced body axis phenotype, and all the epidermal IC progenitors adopted the epidermal SC fate in such a high Notch activity background (Notch-ON embryos). We selected Notch-ON embryos aged at 24 hpf to perform an atp1b1b and ca2a in situ study, and found that only 3% of NaRCs and 1% of HRCs (n = 104, Figure 8C) differentiated. However, when we forced foxi3a expression in Notch-ON embryos, it was sufficient to restore both NaRC (100%, n = 74) and HRC (100%, n = 74) differentiation with high penetrance (Figure 8D). foxi3b, on the contrary, was sufficient to restore full NaRC (100%, n = 86) and partial HRC (24%, n = 86) differentiation in Notch-ON embryos (Figure 8E).
###end p 33
###begin p 34
###xml 48 54 48 54 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">foxi3a</italic>
###xml 59 65 59 65 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">foxi3b</italic>
###xml 69 73 69 73 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">bmp7</italic>
###xml 197 201 197 201 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pone.0000302-Schier1">[45]</xref>
###xml 364 370 364 370 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">foxi3a</italic>
###xml 428 432 428 432 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">bmp7</italic>
###xml 506 507 506 507 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">n</italic>
###xml 527 528 527 528 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">n</italic>
###xml 582 591 582 591 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pone-0000302-g008">Figure 8F</xref>
###xml 649 663 649 663 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">foxi3a in situ</italic>
###xml 712 718 712 718 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">foxi3a</italic>
###xml 733 737 733 737 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">bmp7</italic>
###xml 795 796 795 796 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">n</italic>
###xml 818 819 818 819 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">n</italic>
###xml 864 873 864 873 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pone-0000302-g008">Figure 8G</xref>
###xml 876 882 876 882 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">foxi3b</italic>
###xml 935 936 935 936 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">n</italic>
###xml 968 969 968 969 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">n</italic>
###xml 996 1000 996 1000 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">bmp7</italic>
###xml 1012 1021 1012 1021 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pone-0000302-g008">Figure 8H</xref>
###xml 1322 1333 1322 1333 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">X-Su(H)/Ank</italic>
###xml 1339 1345 1339 1345 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">foxi3b</italic>
###xml 1354 1358 1354 1358 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">bmp7</italic>
###xml 1362 1368 1362 1368 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">foxi3b</italic>
In parallel, we also dissected the functions of foxi3a and foxi3b in bmp7 morphants. Bmp functions as upstream signals, which are essential for ventral cell fate and epidermal ectoderm development [45]. Because epidermal ICs are generated from epidermal SCs, we hypothesized that epidermal IC specification is also regulated by Bmp activity. Indeed, we found that foxi3a expression was very sensitive to Bmp activity. In 24-hpf bmp7 morphants, although we still could detect P63 expression, both NaRC (0%, n = 88) and HRC (0%, n = 88) differentiations were completely undetectable (Figure 8F) due to the loss of epidermal IC identity (detected by a foxi3a in situ study, data not shown). However, when we forced foxi3a expression in bmp7 morphants, it was sufficient to restore both NaRC (100%, n = 62) and HRC (100%, n = 62) differentiation with high penetrance (Figure 8G). foxi3b misexpression was sufficient to restore NaRC (100%, n = 103) and partially HRC (21%, n = 103) differentiation in bmp7 morphants (Figure 8H). Taken together, we concluded that first, either Foxi3a or Foxi3b activity may be sufficient to promote the default fate of NaRC differentiation; second, the alternative fate of HRC differentiation requires a high level of Foxi3a; and third, the partial restoration of HRCs in embryos injected with X-Su(H)/Ank mRNA+foxi3b mRNA or bmp7 MO+foxi3b mRNA may be mediated by Foxi3a activity. And this Foxi3a activity is probably boosted by the Foxi3b feedback regulatory loop.
###end p 34
###begin title 35
Loss-of-Function Assay Suggests that Foxi3a Functions as a Master Regulator to Maintain Epidermal IC Identity and Activate Epidermal IC Differentiation
###end title 35
###begin p 36
###xml 67 73 67 73 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">foxi3a</italic>

###xml 389 392 389 392 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">mis</sup>

###xml 452 461 452 461 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pone.0000302.s004">Figure S4</xref>
###xml 602 611 600 609 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pone-0000302-g009">Figure 9C</xref>
###xml 632 638 630 636 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">foxi3a</italic>
###xml 701 710 699 708 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pone-0000302-g009">Figure 9D</xref>
###xml 751 757 749 755 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">foxi3a</italic>
